### <a id="inductively-defined-closure-operators">Inductively Defined Closure Operators</a>

This section presents the [UALib.Varieties.Varieties][] module of the [Agda Universal Algebra Library][].

A *variety* is a class of algebras (in the same signature) that is closed under the taking of homomorphic images (H), subalgebras (S), and arbitrary products (P).

In this module we present the most useful inductive types that we have found in Martin-LÃ¶f type theory for representing classes of algebras that are closed under H, S, P, and V â‰¡ HSP.

#### S-closure

Similarly, we have found the following to be the most useful inductive type for representing classes of algebras that are closed under the taking of subalgebras.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="1790" class="Comment">--Closure wrt S</a>
<a id="1806" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="S"></a><a id="1811" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#1811" class="Datatype">S</a> <a id="1813" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="1814" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a> <a id="1880" href="Agda.Primitive.html#636" class="Function Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="1882" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#1816" class="Bound">ğ“¦</a><a id="1883" #### P-closure

The most useful inductive type that we have found for representing classes of algebras that are closed under the taking of arbitrary products is the following.

<pre class="Agda">

#### V-closure

Finally, we define an inductive type that represents varieties---classes of algebras closed under the taking of homomorphic images, subalgebras and products.

<pre class="Agda">

#### Closure properties

The types defined above represent operators with useful closure properties. We now prove a handful of such properties since we will need them later.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="4517" class="Comment">-- P is a closure operator, in particular, it&#39;s expansive...</a>
<a id="P-expa"></a><a id="4578" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#4578" class="Function">P-expa</a> <a id="4585" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="4587" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="4588" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#4588" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a> <a id="4590" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="4592" href="universes.html#551" class="Postulate">Universe</a><a id="4600" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="4602" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#4602" class="Bound">ğ’¦</a> <a id="4604" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="4606" href="UALib.Relations.Unary.html#748" class="Function">Pred</a> <a id="4611" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="4612" href="UALib.Algebras.Algebras.html#1471" class="Function">Algebra</a> <a id="4620" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#4588" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a> <a id="4622" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#936" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a><a id="4623" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="4625" href="UALib.Subalgebras.Subalgebras.html#2208" class="Function">OV</a> <a id="4628" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#4588" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a><a id="4629" class="Symbol">)}</a>

#### Some useful tools

We sometimes want to go back and forth between our two representations of subalgebras of algebras in a class. The tools `subalgebraâ†’S` and `Sâ†’subalgebra` are made for that purpose.

</pre>

Next we observe that lifting to a higher universe does not break the property of being a subalgebra of an algebra of a class.  In other words, if we lift a subalgebra of an algebra in a class, the result is still a subalgebra of an algebra in the class.

The next lemma would be too obvoius to care about were it not for the fact that we'll need it later, so it too must be formalized.

We need to formalize one more lemma before arriving the short term objective of this section, which is the proof of the inclusion PSâŠ†SP.

<pre class="Agda">

#### PS(ğ’¦) âŠ† SP(ğ’¦)

Finally, we are in a position to prove that a product of subalgebras of algebras in a class ğ’¦ is a subalgebra of a product of algebras in ğ’¦.

#### More class inclusion lemmas

We conclude this module with three more inclusion relations that will have bit parts to play in our formal proof of Birkhoff's Theorem.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="PâŠ†V"></a><a id="15693" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#15693" class="Function">PâŠ†V</a> <a id="15697" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="15699" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="15700" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#15700" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a> <a id="15702" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#15702" class="Bound">ğ“¦</a> <a id="15704" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="15706" href="universes.html#551" class="Postulate">Universe</a><a id="15714" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="15716" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#15716" class="Bound">ğ’¦</a> <a id="15718" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="15720" href="UALib.Relations.Unary.html#748" class="Function">Pred</a> <a id="15725" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="15726" href="UALib.Algebras.Algebras.html#1471" class="Function">Algebra</a> <a id="15734" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#15700" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a> <a id="15736" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#936" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a><a id="15737" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="15739" href="UALib.Subalgebras.Subalgebras.html#2208" class="Function">OV</a> <a id="15742" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#15700" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a><a id="15743" class="Symbol">)}</a>

</pre>


#### A type for the product of all algebras in a class

Above we proved PS(ğ’¦) âŠ† SP(ğ’¦).  It is slightly more painful to prove that the product of *all* algebras in the class S(ğ’¦) is a member of SP(ğ’¦). That is,

```agda
â¨… S(ğ’¦) âˆˆ SP(ğ’¦)
```

This is mainly due to the fact that it's not obvious (at least not to this author-coder) what should be the type of the product of all members of a class of algebras.  After a few false starts, eventually the right type revealed itself.  Of course, now that we have it in our hands, it seems rather obvious.

We now describe the this type of product of all algebras in an arbitrary class ğ’¦ of algebras of the same signature.

</pre>

Notice that, if `p : ğ‘¨ âˆˆ ğ’¦`, then we can think of the pair `(ğ‘¨ , p) âˆˆ â„‘ ğ’¦` as an index over the class, and so we can think of `ğ”„ (ğ‘¨ , p)` (which is obviously `ğ‘¨`) as the projection of the product `â¨… ( ğ”„{ğ“¤}{ğ’¦} )` onto the `(ğ‘¨ , p)`-th component.

#### â¨… S(ğ’¦) âˆˆ SP(ğ’¦)
Finally, we prove the result that plays a leading role in the formal proof of Birkhoff's Theorem---namely, that our newly defined class product â¨… ( ğ”„{ğ“¤}{ğ’¦} ) belongs to SP(ğ’¦).

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="18569" class="Comment">-- The product of all subalgebras of a class ğ’¦ belongs to SP(ğ’¦).</a>
